	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">List of unusual deaths</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Wikimedia list article</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable plainlinks">This is a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Lists#Incomplete_lists" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Lists">dynamic list</a> and may never be able to satisfy particular standards for completeness. You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_unusual_deaths&amp;action=edit">expanding it</a> with <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources">reliably sourced</a> entries.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Death_of_Aeschylus_in_Florentine_Picture_Chronicle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3a/Death_of_Aeschylus_in_Florentine_Picture_Chronicle.jpg/170px-Death_of_Aeschylus_in_Florentine_Picture_Chronicle.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="265" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3a/Death_of_Aeschylus_in_Florentine_Picture_Chronicle.jpg/255px-Death_of_Aeschylus_in_Florentine_Picture_Chronicle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3a/Death_of_Aeschylus_in_Florentine_Picture_Chronicle.jpg/340px-Death_of_Aeschylus_in_Florentine_Picture_Chronicle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="493" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Death_of_Aeschylus_in_Florentine_Picture_Chronicle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The death of <a href="/wiki/Aeschylus" title="Aeschylus">Aeschylus</a> illustrated in the 15th-century <i>Florentine Picture Chronicle</i> by <a href="/wiki/Maso_Finiguerra" title="Maso Finiguerra">Maso Finiguerra</a><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>This <b>list of unusual deaths</b> includes unique or extremely rare circumstances of death recorded throughout history, noted as being unusual by multiple sources. 
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Antiquity">Antiquity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_unusual_deaths&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Antiquity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Many of these stories are likely to be apocryphal.</div>
<table class="wikitable">

<tbody><tr>
<th style="width:170pt;">Name of person
</th>
<th scope="col">Image
</th>
<th scope="col">Date of death
</th>
<th scope="col">Details
</th></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Sisera" title="Sisera">Sisera</a>
</th>
<td><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Lambert_Lombard,_Ja%C3%ABl_(1530-35),_Grand_Curtius,_Li%C3%A8ge.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Lambert Lombard, Jaël (1530-35), Grand Curtius, Liège.JPG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Lambert_Lombard%2C_Ja%C3%ABl_%281530-35%29%2C_Grand_Curtius%2C_Li%C3%A8ge.JPG/100px-Lambert_Lombard%2C_Ja%C3%ABl_%281530-35%29%2C_Grand_Curtius%2C_Li%C3%A8ge.JPG" decoding="async" width="100" height="109" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Lambert_Lombard%2C_Ja%C3%ABl_%281530-35%29%2C_Grand_Curtius%2C_Li%C3%A8ge.JPG/150px-Lambert_Lombard%2C_Ja%C3%ABl_%281530-35%29%2C_Grand_Curtius%2C_Li%C3%A8ge.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Lambert_Lombard%2C_Ja%C3%ABl_%281530-35%29%2C_Grand_Curtius%2C_Li%C3%A8ge.JPG/200px-Lambert_Lombard%2C_Ja%C3%ABl_%281530-35%29%2C_Grand_Curtius%2C_Li%C3%A8ge.JPG 2x" data-file-width="802" data-file-height="877" /></a></div></div>
</td>
<td>13th century BCE
</td>
<td><b>Sisera</b> (<a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">Hebrew</a>: <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r940540609">.mw-parser-output .script-hebrew,.mw-parser-output .script-Hebr{font-size:1.15em;font-family:"SBL Hebrew","SBL BibLit","Frank Ruehl CLM","Taamey Frank CLM","Ezra SIL","Ezra SIL SR","Keter Aram Tsova","Taamey Ashkenaz","Taamey David CLM","Keter YG","Shofar","David CLM","Hadasim CLM","Simple CLM","Nachlieli",Cardo,Alef,"Noto Serif Hebrew","Noto Sans Hebrew","David Libre",David,"Times New Roman",Gisha,Arial,FreeSerif,FreeSans}</style><span class="script-hebrew" style="font-size: 115%;" dir="rtl">סִיסְרָא</span> <i>Sîsərā</i>) was commander of the <a href="/wiki/Canaanite_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Canaanite peoples">Canaanite</a> army of King <a href="/wiki/Jabin" title="Jabin">Jabin</a> of <a href="/wiki/Tel_Hazor" title="Tel Hazor">Hazor</a>, who is mentioned in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.biblica.com/bible/?osis=niv:Judges.4–5">Judges 4-5</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_Bible" title="Hebrew Bible">Hebrew Bible</a>. After being defeated by the forces of the Israelite tribes of <a href="/wiki/Zebulun" title="Zebulun">Zebulun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Naphtali" title="Naphtali">Naphtali</a> under the command of <a href="/wiki/Barak" title="Barak">Barak</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deborah" title="Deborah">Deborah</a>, Sisera was killed by <a href="/wiki/Jael" title="Jael">Jael</a>, who hammered a tent peg into his <a href="/wiki/Temple_(anatomy)" title="Temple (anatomy)">temple</a>.
<p><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Draco_(lawgiver)" title="Draco (lawgiver)">Draco</a> of Athens
</th>
<td>
</td>
<td><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 620 BC
</td>
<td>Draco, an Athenian lawmaker, was reportedly smothered to death by gifts of cloaks and hats showered upon him by appreciative citizens at a theatre on <a href="/wiki/Aegina" title="Aegina">Aegina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Charondas" title="Charondas">Charondas</a>
</th>
<td><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Illustration_of_the_death_of_Charondas_from_1787.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Illustration of the death of Charondas from 1787.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Illustration_of_the_death_of_Charondas_from_1787.jpg/100px-Illustration_of_the_death_of_Charondas_from_1787.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Illustration_of_the_death_of_Charondas_from_1787.jpg/150px-Illustration_of_the_death_of_Charondas_from_1787.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Illustration_of_the_death_of_Charondas_from_1787.jpg/200px-Illustration_of_the_death_of_Charondas_from_1787.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1807" data-file-height="2403" /></a></div></div>
</td>
<td>Late 7th to early 5th century BC
</td>
<td>Charondas was a Greek lawgiver from <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Murray2007_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murray2007-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-McGlew1993_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McGlew1993-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Diodorus_Siculus" title="Diodorus Siculus">Diodorus Siculus</a>, he issued a law that anyone who brought weapons into the <a href="/wiki/Ecclesia_(ancient_Athens)" title="Ecclesia (ancient Athens)">Assembly</a> must be put to death.<sup id="cite_ref-Murray2007_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murray2007-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-McGlew1993_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McGlew1993-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Groebner2002_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Groebner2002-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> One day, he arrived at the Assembly seeking help to defeat some brigands in the countryside but with a knife still attached to his belt.<sup id="cite_ref-Murray2007_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murray2007-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-McGlew1993_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McGlew1993-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In order to uphold his own law, he committed suicide.<sup id="cite_ref-Murray2007_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murray2007-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-McGlew1993_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McGlew1993-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Groebner2002_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Groebner2002-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Arrhichion" title="Arrhichion">Arrhichion</a> of <a href="/wiki/Phigalia" title="Phigalia">Phigalia</a>
</th>
<td><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Pankratiasten_in_fight_greek_statue_2_century_bC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Pankratiasten in fight greek statue 2 century bC.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Pankratiasten_in_fight_greek_statue_2_century_bC.jpg/100px-Pankratiasten_in_fight_greek_statue_2_century_bC.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="143" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Pankratiasten_in_fight_greek_statue_2_century_bC.jpg/150px-Pankratiasten_in_fight_greek_statue_2_century_bC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Pankratiasten_in_fight_greek_statue_2_century_bC.jpg/200px-Pankratiasten_in_fight_greek_statue_2_century_bC.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1884" data-file-height="2693" /></a></div></div>
</td>
<td>564 BC
</td>
<td>Arrichion of Phigalia, a Greek <a href="/wiki/Pankration" title="Pankration">pankratiast</a>, caused his own death during the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Olympic_Games" title="Ancient Olympic Games">Olympic</a> finals. Held by his unidentified opponent in a stranglehold and unable to free himself, Arrichion kicked his opponent, causing him so much pain that the opponent made the sign of defeat to the umpires, but at the same time broke Arrichion's neck. Since the opponent had conceded defeat, Arrichion was proclaimed the victor posthumously.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th><a href="/wiki/Sisamnes" title="Sisamnes">Sisamnes</a>
</th>
<td><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Gerard_David_-_The_Judgment_of_Cambyses,_panel_2_-_The_shedding_of_the_corrupt_judge_Sisamnes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Gerard David - The Judgment of Cambyses, panel 2 - The shedding of the corrupt judge Sisamnes.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Gerard_David_-_The_Judgment_of_Cambyses%2C_panel_2_-_The_shedding_of_the_corrupt_judge_Sisamnes.jpg/100px-Gerard_David_-_The_Judgment_of_Cambyses%2C_panel_2_-_The_shedding_of_the_corrupt_judge_Sisamnes.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="116" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Gerard_David_-_The_Judgment_of_Cambyses%2C_panel_2_-_The_shedding_of_the_corrupt_judge_Sisamnes.jpg/149px-Gerard_David_-_The_Judgment_of_Cambyses%2C_panel_2_-_The_shedding_of_the_corrupt_judge_Sisamnes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Gerard_David_-_The_Judgment_of_Cambyses%2C_panel_2_-_The_shedding_of_the_corrupt_judge_Sisamnes.jpg/199px-Gerard_David_-_The_Judgment_of_Cambyses%2C_panel_2_-_The_shedding_of_the_corrupt_judge_Sisamnes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5122" data-file-height="5960" /></a></div></div>
</td>
<td>c. 525 BC
</td>
<td>According to <a href="/wiki/Herodotus" title="Herodotus">Herodotus</a>, Sisamnes was a corrupt judge under <a href="/wiki/Cambyses_II" title="Cambyses II">Cambyses II of Persia</a>. He accepted a bribe and delivered an unjust verdict. As a result, the king had him arrested and <a href="/wiki/Flaying" title="Flaying">flayed alive</a>. His skin was then used to cover the seat in which his son would sit in judgment.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Pythagoras" title="Pythagoras">Pythagoras</a> of <a href="/wiki/Samos" title="Samos">Samos</a>
</th>
<td><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Kapitolinischer_Pythagoras_adjusted.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Kapitolinischer Pythagoras adjusted.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Kapitolinischer_Pythagoras_adjusted.jpg/100px-Kapitolinischer_Pythagoras_adjusted.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Kapitolinischer_Pythagoras_adjusted.jpg/150px-Kapitolinischer_Pythagoras_adjusted.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Kapitolinischer_Pythagoras_adjusted.jpg/200px-Kapitolinischer_Pythagoras_adjusted.jpg 2x" data-file-width="449" data-file-height="599" /></a></div></div>
</td>
<td><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 495 BC
</td>
<td>Ancient sources disagree on how the Greek philosopher <a href="/wiki/Pythagoras" title="Pythagoras">Pythagoras</a> died,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Simoons1998_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Simoons1998-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> but one late and probably apocryphal legend reported by both <a href="/wiki/Diogenes_La%C3%ABrtius" title="Diogenes Laërtius">Diogenes Laërtius</a>, a third-century AD biographer of famous philosophers, and <a href="/wiki/Iamblichus" title="Iamblichus">Iamblichus</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Neoplatonism" title="Neoplatonism">Neoplatonist</a> philosopher, states that Pythagoras was murdered by his political enemies.<sup id="cite_ref-Simoons1998_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Simoons1998-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Supposedly, he almost managed to outrun them,<sup id="cite_ref-Simoons1998_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Simoons1998-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> but he came to a bean field and refused to run through it because he had prohibited beans as ritually unclean.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Simoons1998_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Simoons1998-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Since cutting through the field would violate his own <a href="/wiki/Pythagoreanism" title="Pythagoreanism">teachings</a>, Pythagoras simply stopped running and was killed.<sup id="cite_ref-Simoons1998_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Simoons1998-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> This story may have been fabricated by <a href="/wiki/Neanthes_of_Cyzicus" title="Neanthes of Cyzicus">Neanthes of Cyzicus</a>, on whom both Diogenes and Iamblichus rely as a source.<sup id="cite_ref-Simoons1998_13-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Simoons1998-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Heraclitus" title="Heraclitus">Heraclitus</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ephesus" title="Ephesus">Ephesus</a>
</th>
<td><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Utrecht_Moreelse_Heraclite.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Utrecht Moreelse Heraclite.JPG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Utrecht_Moreelse_Heraclite.JPG/100px-Utrecht_Moreelse_Heraclite.JPG" decoding="async" width="100" height="82" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Utrecht_Moreelse_Heraclite.JPG/150px-Utrecht_Moreelse_Heraclite.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Utrecht_Moreelse_Heraclite.JPG/200px-Utrecht_Moreelse_Heraclite.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1900" data-file-height="1564" /></a></div></div>
</td>
<td><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 475 BC
</td>
<td>According to one account given by Diogenes Laërtius, the Greek philosopher Heraclitus was said to have been devoured by dogs after smearing himself with cow manure in an attempt to cure his <a href="/wiki/Dropsy" class="mw-redirect" title="Dropsy">dropsy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Johnston1806a_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johnston1806a-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Themistocles" title="Themistocles">Themistocles</a>
</th>
<td><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Busto_di_temistocle,_da_originale_greco_del_V_secolo_ac,_dal_decumano_presso_il_casamento_del_temistocle.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Busto di temistocle, da originale greco del V secolo ac, dal decumano presso il casamento del temistocle.JPG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Busto_di_temistocle%2C_da_originale_greco_del_V_secolo_ac%2C_dal_decumano_presso_il_casamento_del_temistocle.JPG/100px-Busto_di_temistocle%2C_da_originale_greco_del_V_secolo_ac%2C_dal_decumano_presso_il_casamento_del_temistocle.JPG" decoding="async" width="100" height="159" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Busto_di_temistocle%2C_da_originale_greco_del_V_secolo_ac%2C_dal_decumano_presso_il_casamento_del_temistocle.JPG/150px-Busto_di_temistocle%2C_da_originale_greco_del_V_secolo_ac%2C_dal_decumano_presso_il_casamento_del_temistocle.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Busto_di_temistocle%2C_da_originale_greco_del_V_secolo_ac%2C_dal_decumano_presso_il_casamento_del_temistocle.JPG/200px-Busto_di_temistocle%2C_da_originale_greco_del_V_secolo_ac%2C_dal_decumano_presso_il_casamento_del_temistocle.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2624" data-file-height="4168" /></a></div></div>
</td>
<td><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 459 BC
</td>
<td>Themistocles, the Athenian general who won the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Salamis" title="Battle of Salamis">Battle of Salamis</a>, actually died of natural causes in exile,<sup id="cite_ref-TI138_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TI138-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Marr_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marr-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> but was widely rumored to have committed suicide by drinking <a href="/wiki/Bull%27s_blood" class="mw-redirect" title="Bull&#39;s blood">bull's blood</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TI138_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TI138-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Marr_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marr-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PT31_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PT31-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DSXI58_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DSXI58-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Since bull's blood is not actually poisonous,<sup id="cite_ref-Marr_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marr-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Themistocles cannot have died in this way,<sup id="cite_ref-Marr_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marr-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> but the legend is widely retold in classical sources.<sup id="cite_ref-Marr_18-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marr-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The early twentieth-century English classicist <a href="/wiki/Percy_Gardner" title="Percy Gardner">Percy Gardner</a> proposed that the story about him drinking bull's blood may have been based on an ignorant misunderstanding of a statue showing Themistocles in a heroic pose, holding a cup as an offering to the gods.<sup id="cite_ref-Marr_18-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marr-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The comedic playwright <a href="/wiki/Aristophanes" title="Aristophanes">Aristophanes</a> references Themistocles drinking bull's blood in his comedy <i><a href="/wiki/The_Knights" title="The Knights">The Knights</a></i> (performed in 324 BC) as the most heroic way for a man to die.<sup id="cite_ref-Marr_18-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marr-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Aeschylus" title="Aeschylus">Aeschylus</a>
</th>
<td><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Herma_of_Aeschylus,_Klas08.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Herma of Aeschylus, Klas08.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Herma_of_Aeschylus%2C_Klas08.jpg/100px-Herma_of_Aeschylus%2C_Klas08.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="148" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Herma_of_Aeschylus%2C_Klas08.jpg/150px-Herma_of_Aeschylus%2C_Klas08.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Herma_of_Aeschylus%2C_Klas08.jpg/200px-Herma_of_Aeschylus%2C_Klas08.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2181" data-file-height="3229" /></a></div></div>
</td>
<td><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 455 BC
</td>
<td>According to <a href="/wiki/Valerius_Maximus" title="Valerius Maximus">Valerius Maximus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aeschylus" title="Aeschylus">Aeschylus</a>, the eldest of the three great Athenian <a href="/wiki/Tragedy" title="Tragedy">tragedians</a>, was killed by a <a href="/wiki/Tortoise" title="Tortoise">tortoise</a> dropped by an eagle that had mistaken his bald head for a rock suitable for shattering the shell of the reptile. <a href="/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder" title="Pliny the Elder">Pliny</a>, in his <i><a href="/wiki/Natural_History_(Pliny)" title="Natural History (Pliny)">Naturalis Historiæ</a></i>, adds that Aeschylus had been staying outdoors to avert a prophecy that he would be killed by a falling object.<sup id="cite_ref-McKeown2013_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKeown2013-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tortue_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tortue-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Empedocles" title="Empedocles">Empedocles</a> of <a href="/wiki/Agrigento" title="Agrigento">Akragas</a>
</th>
<td><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Empedocles_in_Thomas_Stanley_History_of_Philosophy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Empedocles in Thomas Stanley History of Philosophy.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Empedocles_in_Thomas_Stanley_History_of_Philosophy.jpg/100px-Empedocles_in_Thomas_Stanley_History_of_Philosophy.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="144" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Empedocles_in_Thomas_Stanley_History_of_Philosophy.jpg/150px-Empedocles_in_Thomas_Stanley_History_of_Philosophy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Empedocles_in_Thomas_Stanley_History_of_Philosophy.jpg/200px-Empedocles_in_Thomas_Stanley_History_of_Philosophy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="1300" /></a></div></div>
</td>
<td><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 430 BC
</td>
<td>Empedocles of Acragas was a <a href="/wiki/Pre-Socratic_philosophy" title="Pre-Socratic philosophy">Pre-Socratic philosopher</a> from the island of <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a>, who, in one of his surviving poems, declares himself to have become a "<a href="/wiki/Daemon_(classical_mythology)" title="Daemon (classical mythology)">divine being</a>... no longer mortal".<sup id="cite_ref-Gregory_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gregory-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> According to Diogenes Laërtius, he tried to prove he was an immortal god by leaping into <a href="/wiki/Mount_Etna" title="Mount Etna">Mount Etna</a>, an active volcano.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> This legend is also alluded to by the Roman poet <a href="/wiki/Horace" title="Horace">Horace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Sophocles" title="Sophocles">Sophocles</a>
</th>
<td><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Sophocles_pushkin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Sophocles pushkin.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Sophocles_pushkin.jpg/100px-Sophocles_pushkin.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="136" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Sophocles_pushkin.jpg/150px-Sophocles_pushkin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Sophocles_pushkin.jpg/200px-Sophocles_pushkin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="779" data-file-height="1058" /></a></div></div>
</td>
<td><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 406 BC
</td>
<td>A number of "remarkable" legends concerning the death of Sophocles, another of the three great Athenian tragedians, are recorded in the late antique <i>Life of Sophocles</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-McKeown2013_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKeown2013-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> According to one legend, he choked to death on an unripe grape.<sup id="cite_ref-McKeown2013_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKeown2013-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Another says that he died of joy after hearing that his last play had been victorious.<sup id="cite_ref-McKeown2013_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKeown2013-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> A third account reports that he died of suffocation after reading aloud a lengthy monologue from the end of his play <i><a href="/wiki/Antigone_(Sophocles_play)" title="Antigone (Sophocles play)">Antigone</a></i> without pausing to take a breath for commas or punctuation.<sup id="cite_ref-McKeown2013_22-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKeown2013-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Mithridates_(soldier)" title="Mithridates (soldier)">Mithridates</a>
</th>
<td>
</td>
<td>401 BC
</td>
<td>Mithridates, a Persian soldier who embarrassed his king, <a href="/wiki/Artaxerxes_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Artaxerxes II">Artaxerxes II</a>, by boasting of killing his rival, <a href="/wiki/Cyrus_the_Younger" title="Cyrus the Younger">Cyrus the Younger</a> (who was the brother of Artaxerxes II), was executed by <a href="/wiki/Scaphism" title="Scaphism">scaphism</a>. The king's physician, <a href="/wiki/Ctesias" title="Ctesias">Ctesias</a>, reported that Mithridates survived the insect torture for 17 days.<sup id="cite_ref-10tbd_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10tbd-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-acogc_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-acogc-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Democritus" title="Democritus">Democritus</a> of <a href="/wiki/Abdera,_Thrace" title="Abdera, Thrace">Abdera</a>
</th>
<td><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Hendrik_ter_Brugghen_-_Democritus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Hendrik ter Brugghen - Democritus.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Hendrik_ter_Brugghen_-_Democritus.jpg/100px-Hendrik_ter_Brugghen_-_Democritus.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="124" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Hendrik_ter_Brugghen_-_Democritus.jpg/150px-Hendrik_ter_Brugghen_-_Democritus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Hendrik_ter_Brugghen_-_Democritus.jpg/200px-Hendrik_ter_Brugghen_-_Democritus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1291" data-file-height="1600" /></a></div></div>
</td>
<td><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 370 BC
</td>
<td>According to Diogenes Laërtius, the Greek <a href="/wiki/Atomism" title="Atomism">Atomist</a> philosopher Democritus of Abdera died at the age of 109;<sup id="cite_ref-McKeown2013p157_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKeown2013p157-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Diogenesix43_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Diogenesix43-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> as he was on his deathbed, his sister was greatly worried because she needed to fulfill her religious obligations to the goddess <a href="/wiki/Artemis" title="Artemis">Artemis</a> in the approaching three-day <a href="/wiki/Thesmophoria" title="Thesmophoria">Thesmophoria</a> festival.<sup id="cite_ref-McKeown2013p157_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKeown2013p157-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Diogenesix43_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Diogenesix43-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Democritus told her to place a loaf of warm bread under his nose<sup id="cite_ref-McKeown2013p157_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKeown2013p157-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Diogenesix43_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Diogenesix43-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> and was able to survive for the three days of the festival by sniffing it.<sup id="cite_ref-McKeown2013p157_31-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKeown2013p157-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Diogenesix43_32-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Diogenesix43-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> He died immediately after the festival was over.<sup id="cite_ref-McKeown2013p157_31-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McKeown2013p157-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Diogenesix43_32-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Diogenesix43-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th><a href="/wiki/Antiphanes_(comic_poet)" title="Antiphanes (comic poet)">Antiphanes</a>
</th>
<td>
</td>
<td>c. 310 BC
</td>
<td>Antiphanes was a renowned comic poet of the Middle <a href="/wiki/Attic_comedy" class="mw-redirect" title="Attic comedy">Attic comedy</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Suda" title="Suda">Suda</a> claims he died after being struck by a pear.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Agathocles_of_Syracuse" title="Agathocles of Syracuse">Agathocles of Syracuse</a>
</th>
<td><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Siracusa,_agatocle,_25_litre,_310-300_ac_ca.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Siracusa, agatocle, 25 litre, 310-300 ac ca.JPG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Siracusa%2C_agatocle%2C_25_litre%2C_310-300_ac_ca.JPG/100px-Siracusa%2C_agatocle%2C_25_litre%2C_310-300_ac_ca.JPG" decoding="async" width="100" height="99" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Siracusa%2C_agatocle%2C_25_litre%2C_310-300_ac_ca.JPG/150px-Siracusa%2C_agatocle%2C_25_litre%2C_310-300_ac_ca.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Siracusa%2C_agatocle%2C_25_litre%2C_310-300_ac_ca.JPG/200px-Siracusa%2C_agatocle%2C_25_litre%2C_310-300_ac_ca.JPG 2x" data-file-width="588" data-file-height="584" /></a></div></div>
</td>
<td>289 BC
</td>
<td>Agathocles, a Greek <a href="/wiki/Tyrant" title="Tyrant">tyrant</a> of <a href="/wiki/Syracuse,_Sicily" title="Syracuse, Sicily">Syracuse</a>, was murdered with a poisoned toothpick.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Philitas_of_Cos" title="Philitas of Cos">Philitas of Cos</a>
</th>
<td><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Antikythera_philosopher.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Antikythera philosopher.JPG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Antikythera_philosopher.JPG/100px-Antikythera_philosopher.JPG" decoding="async" width="100" height="124" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Antikythera_philosopher.JPG/150px-Antikythera_philosopher.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Antikythera_philosopher.JPG/200px-Antikythera_philosopher.JPG 2x" data-file-width="699" data-file-height="864" /></a></div></div>
</td>
<td><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 270 BC
</td>
<td>Philitas of Cos, a Greek intellectual, is said by <a href="/wiki/Athenaeus" title="Athenaeus">Athenaeus</a> to have studied arguments and erroneous word usage so intensely that he wasted away and starved to death.<sup id="cite_ref-9.401e_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9.401e-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> British classicist <a href="/wiki/Alan_Cameron_(classical_scholar)" title="Alan Cameron (classical scholar)">Alan Cameron</a> speculates that Philitas died from a <a href="/wiki/Wasting" title="Wasting">wasting</a> disease which his contemporaries joked was caused by his <a href="/wiki/Pedant" title="Pedant">pedantry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Qin_Shi_Huang" title="Qin Shi Huang">Qin Shi Huang</a>
</th>
<td><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Qinshihuang.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Qinshihuang.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Qinshihuang.jpg/100px-Qinshihuang.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="128" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Qinshihuang.jpg/150px-Qinshihuang.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Qinshihuang.jpg/200px-Qinshihuang.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1732" data-file-height="2220" /></a></div></div>
</td>
<td>10 September 210 BC
</td>
<td>Qin Shi Huang, the first <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_China" title="Emperor of China">Emperor of China</a>, whose artifacts and treasures include the <a href="/wiki/Terracotta_Army" title="Terracotta Army">Terracotta Army</a>, died after ingesting several pills of <a href="/wiki/Mercury_poisoning" title="Mercury poisoning">mercury</a> in the belief that it would grant him <a href="/wiki/Immortality" title="Immortality">eternal life</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Nate_Hopper_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nate_Hopper-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Chrysippus" title="Chrysippus">Chrysippus</a> of Soli
</th>
<td><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Chrysippos_BM_1846.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Chrysippos BM 1846.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Chrysippos_BM_1846.jpg/100px-Chrysippos_BM_1846.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="125" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Chrysippos_BM_1846.jpg/150px-Chrysippos_BM_1846.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Chrysippos_BM_1846.jpg/200px-Chrysippos_BM_1846.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2640" data-file-height="3300" /></a></div></div>
</td>
<td><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 206 BC
</td>
<td>One ancient account of the death of Chrysippus, a third-century BC <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Greek</a> <a href="/wiki/Stoicism" title="Stoicism">Stoic</a> philosopher, tells that he <a href="/wiki/Death_from_laughter" title="Death from laughter">died of laughter</a> after he saw a <a href="/wiki/Donkey" title="Donkey">donkey</a> eating his <a href="/wiki/Common_fig" title="Common fig">figs</a>; he told a slave to give the donkey neat wine to drink to wash them down with, and then, "...having laughed too much, he died" (Diogenes Laërtius 7.185).<sup id="cite_ref-Chrysippus_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chrysippus-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Eleazar_Avaran" title="Eleazar Avaran">Eleazar Avaran</a>
</th>
<td><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Harley3240_f.28_ElephantDetail.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Harley3240 f.28 ElephantDetail.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Harley3240_f.28_ElephantDetail.jpg/100px-Harley3240_f.28_ElephantDetail.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="99" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Harley3240_f.28_ElephantDetail.jpg/150px-Harley3240_f.28_ElephantDetail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Harley3240_f.28_ElephantDetail.jpg/200px-Harley3240_f.28_ElephantDetail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="491" data-file-height="486" /></a></div></div>
</td>
<td><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 163 BC
</td>
<td>Eleazar Avaran was the brother of <a href="/wiki/Judas_Maccabeus" title="Judas Maccabeus">Judas Maccabeus</a>. According to <a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Translation:1_Maccabees" class="extiw" title="wikisource:Translation:1 Maccabees">1 Maccabees 6:46</a>, in battle, he thrust his spear into the belly of a king's <a href="/wiki/War_elephant" title="War elephant">war elephant</a>, which collapsed and fell on top of Eleazar, killing him instantly.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th><a href="/wiki/Porcia_(wife_of_Brutus)" title="Porcia (wife of Brutus)">Porcia Catonis</a>
</th>
<td><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Le_Suicide_de_Porcia.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Le Suicide de Porcia.JPG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Le_Suicide_de_Porcia.JPG/100px-Le_Suicide_de_Porcia.JPG" decoding="async" width="100" height="124" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Le_Suicide_de_Porcia.JPG/150px-Le_Suicide_de_Porcia.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Le_Suicide_de_Porcia.JPG/200px-Le_Suicide_de_Porcia.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2735" data-file-height="3398" /></a></div></div>
</td>
<td>June 43 to October 42 BC
</td>
<td>The daughter of <a href="/wiki/Cato_the_Younger" title="Cato the Younger">Marcus Porcius Cato Uticensis</a> and second wife of <a href="/wiki/Brutus_the_Younger" class="mw-redirect" title="Brutus the Younger">Marcus Junius Brutus</a>, according to ancient historians such as <a href="/wiki/Cassius_Dio" title="Cassius Dio">Cassius Dio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Appian" title="Appian">Appian</a> killed herself by swallowing hot coals.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Modern historians find this tale implausible.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th><a href="/wiki/Claudius_Drusus" title="Claudius Drusus">Claudius Drusus</a>
</th>
<td>
</td>
<td>c. 20 AD
</td>
<td>According to <a href="/wiki/Suetonius" title="Suetonius">Suetonius</a>, Claudius Drusus, the eldest son of the future <a href="/wiki/Roman_emperor" title="Roman emperor">Roman Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Claudius" title="Claudius">Claudius</a>, died while playing. Having tossed a pear high in the air, when it came back, he caught it in his mouth but he choked on it, dying of <a href="/wiki/Asphyxia" title="Asphyxia">asphyxia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th><a href="/wiki/Tiberius" title="Tiberius">Tiberius</a>
</th>
<td><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:JPaul_Laurens_The_Death_of_Tiberius.jpg" class="image"><img alt="JPaul Laurens The Death of Tiberius.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/JPaul_Laurens_The_Death_of_Tiberius.jpg/100px-JPaul_Laurens_The_Death_of_Tiberius.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="77" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/JPaul_Laurens_The_Death_of_Tiberius.jpg/150px-JPaul_Laurens_The_Death_of_Tiberius.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/JPaul_Laurens_The_Death_of_Tiberius.jpg/200px-JPaul_Laurens_The_Death_of_Tiberius.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1001" data-file-height="775" /></a></div></div>
</td>
<td>16 March 37 AD
</td>
<td>The Roman emperor Tiberius died in <a href="/wiki/Miseno" title="Miseno">Misenum</a> at the age of seventy-eight. According to <a href="/wiki/Tacitus" title="Tacitus">Tacitus</a>, the emperor appeared to have died and <a href="/wiki/Caligula" title="Caligula">Caligula</a>, who was at Tiberius' villa, was being congratulated on his succession to the empire, when news arrived that the emperor had revived and was recovering his faculties. Those who had moments before recognized Caligula as <a href="/wiki/Augustus_(title)" title="Augustus (title)">Augustus</a> fled in fear of the emperor's wrath, while <a href="/wiki/Naevius_Sutorius_Macro" title="Naevius Sutorius Macro">Macro</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Praetorian_prefect" title="Praetorian prefect">prefect</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Praetorian_Guard" title="Praetorian Guard">Praetorian Guard</a>, took advantage of the chaos to have Tiberius smothered with his own bedclothes, definitively killing him.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th><a href="/wiki/Simon_the_Zealot" title="Simon the Zealot">Simon the Zealot</a>
</th>
<td><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Zers%C3%A4gen_des_Heiligen_Simon.png" class="image"><img alt="Zersägen des Heiligen Simon.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Zers%C3%A4gen_des_Heiligen_Simon.png/100px-Zers%C3%A4gen_des_Heiligen_Simon.png" decoding="async" width="100" height="228" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Zers%C3%A4gen_des_Heiligen_Simon.png/150px-Zers%C3%A4gen_des_Heiligen_Simon.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Zers%C3%A4gen_des_Heiligen_Simon.png/200px-Zers%C3%A4gen_des_Heiligen_Simon.png 2x" data-file-width="1306" data-file-height="2980" /></a></div></div>
</td>
<td>1st century AD
</td>
<td>According to an ancient tradition, Simon, an <a href="/wiki/Apostles" title="Apostles">apostle of Jesus</a>, was <a href="/wiki/Death_by_sawing" title="Death by sawing">sawn in half</a> in <a href="/wiki/Parthian_Empire" title="Parthian Empire">Persia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence" title="Saint Lawrence">Saint Lawrence</a>
</th>
<td><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Martyrdom_of_Lawrence_-_Edited.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Martyrdom of Lawrence - Edited.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/58/Martyrdom_of_Lawrence_-_Edited.jpg/100px-Martyrdom_of_Lawrence_-_Edited.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="131" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/58/Martyrdom_of_Lawrence_-_Edited.jpg/150px-Martyrdom_of_Lawrence_-_Edited.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/58/Martyrdom_of_Lawrence_-_Edited.jpg/200px-Martyrdom_of_Lawrence_-_Edited.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1139" data-file-height="1495" /></a></div></div>
</td>
<td>258 AD
</td>
<td>The <a href="/wiki/Deacon" title="Deacon">deacon</a> Saint Lawrence was roasted alive on a giant grill during the persecution of <a href="/wiki/Valerian_(emperor)" title="Valerian (emperor)">Valerian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Prudentius" title="Prudentius">Prudentius</a> tells that he joked with his tormentors, "Turn me over—I'm done on this side".<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> He is now the <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saint</a> of cooks, chefs and comedians.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_unusual_deaths&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
